Divine Decree
advanced
15 min
Power is Created for One Specific Action
Maturidi argues that power is created for a single purpose and cannot be turned to its opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that divine power is created for a single intended action and cannot be redirected to its opposite.

Core Idea
Divine power is like a sword: made for one purpose, not neutral.

Maturidi addresses a critical question in qadar: if God creates power for an action, can that power be used for its opposite? He argues that power is created specifically for one intended act, using the analogy of a sword and dirham. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the refutations of common objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Get a sense of the back-and-forth objections and responses.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail on first read.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the statement that power is created for one action, not both. Look for the phrase 'القدرة مخلوقة لأحدهما لا لهما'.
3
Analyze the sword and dirham analogy
Notice how the sword can be used for good or evil, but it was created for a specific purpose. Maturidi uses this to show that power is not neutral.
The analogy appears multiple times.
4
Follow the objections and refutations
The passage addresses: (1) why power isn't 'strengthened' for one, (2) why the sinner's action isn't by God's power, (3) how power can be turned. See how Maturidi answers each.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Conclude that power is created for one of the two opposites (good or evil) and cannot be turned. Why does this matter for understanding divine justice?
This connects to the broader theme of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعارضته بالله سبحانه محال على القولين: على قولنا بأنه خالق بذاته فالقول به كالقول بأنه لم قدر وعلم؟ وعلى قوله إن ذلك أصلح في الدين، ولا يُسأل من ذلك وصف فعله، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ونحن نحمد الله، قد أغنانا الله عن نحو هذا السؤال، لكن أحببت أن أذكرهما مقداره فما لا يرضى به سؤالا لضعفه؛ ليعلموا به قدره في المرضى به، والله الموفق. أنه إذ صلحت قوة واحدة للإيمان وضده ليم لا صلح القول بالتقوية عليها، فدفع ذا بالأمر والنهى: وعارض بالسيف والدرهم وإن احتمل استعماله فى قتل الولى وانفاقه فى شرى الخمر، لم يجز القول بالإعطاء لذلك. نقول: تمام السؤال أن الله إذ علم أنه فيم يستعمل يستعمل، وفى مثله فى الشاهد يوصف بالتقوية عليه، والله لم يوصف بمثله، فمثله في الخلق مع ما يقال بالأول، لكنه طلب منه، واختيار ذلك فيه لا بها، ولا يُوضع في ذلك حرف الإعطاء؛ لأنه امتنان، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما عارض فاسد؛ لاحتماله أن لا يستعمل في الوجهين، فلم يكن الدفع لوجه من ذلك، والقوة لا تحتمل إلا أحدهما، ولا يجوز أن يخلو عن وقوع أحدهما بها، وقد علم بذلك، فلا يحتمل القول بالدفع لغير ذلك. ثم قال: فإن قلت: العاصى إذ يفعل بقدرة الله لم لا قلت: إن المعصية من الله؟ الله: وقد أخطأ قال الشيخ رحمه من وجهين: أحدهما أن خصومه لا يقولون في المعصية إنها من الله، والثانى لا يقال فعل العبد بقدرة الله، ولكن بقدرة طلبها من الله. ثم أجاب في ذلك بمثل جوابه فى الأول: إنه أعطى ليطيع وأتم هذا، وقد بينا الوجه في الأول وخطأه في هذا السؤال. ثم عارض نفسه بما إذ كانت القدرة مخلوقة للخير كيف قدر العبد على قلبها؟ أن ذا ليس كالذي يسخن ويبرد، لكنه كالسيف والدرهم. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: فيقال له: القدرة إذ لا تحتمل الفعلين ولا تركها، وما عارضت به محتمل، ثبت أن القدرة مخلوقة لأحدهما لا لهما، ثم لا يحتمل المخلوق بجهة واحدة قلبها عنها من نحو الذي ذكرت مما يسخن به ويبرد، ليم لا دل أنها وهو ما كان بها، ويبين لك العرف الظاهر في الخلق بسؤال القوة على الخير، ولو كانت لا تحتمل الشر لكان لا معنى لتخصيص ذلك، خلقت لأحدهما، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم عارض نفسه بالغنى، فقال: معاذ الله؛ لأنه المغنى. وعارض بالسيف والدرهم.
And his opposition concerning God—Exalted is He—is impossible on both views: on our view that He is Creator by His essence, then it is like saying why He decreed and knew? And on his view that it is more beneficial for religion, and He is not asked about the description of His action, and there is no power except with God. And we praise God; God has sufficed us from such a question, but I wanted to mention its extent so that they may know his standing in what he is pleased with, and God grants success. That when one power is suitable for faith and its opposite, why is it not suitable to say it is strengthened upon it? He repelled this with command and prohibition: and he opposed with the sword and the dirham, even if its use is possible in killing the friend and spending on buying wine, it is not permissible to say that giving is for that. We say: the complete question is that God, since He knows how it will be used, it is used, and in its like in the witnessed world one is described as strengthening upon it, and God is not described with its like, then its like in creation is with what was said first, but He requested it, and the choice of that is not through it, and the letter of giving is not placed in that; because it is grace, and there is no power except with God. And the opposition is corrupt; because it is possible that it is not used in both ways, so the repulsion was not for a particular aspect, and the power does not admit except one of them, and it is not permissible that it be devoid of one of them occurring by it, and that is known, so it is not plausible to say repulsion for other than that. Then he said: so if you say: the sinner acts with the power of God, why do you not say that sin is from God? God: and he erred, the shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said from two aspects: one is that his opponents do not say that sin is from God, and the second is that the action of the servant is not said to be by the power of God, but by the power he requested from God. Then he answered that with an answer like his first: he gave it so that he might obey, and he completed this, and we have clarified the aspect in the first and his error in this question. Then he opposed himself with: when power is created for good, how is the servant able to turn it? That this is not like that which heats and cools, but it is like the sword and the dirham. Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: so it is said to him: since power does not admit both actions nor their abandonment, and what you opposed with is possible, it is established that power is created for one of them, not for both, then what is created in one aspect cannot be turned away from it like what you mentioned of that which heats and cools, unless it indicates that it is what it was with, and the manifest custom in creation demonstrates to you by asking for power for good, and if it did not admit evil, there would be no meaning to specifying that, it was created for one of them, and there is no power except with God. Then he opposed himself with wealth, and said: God forbid; because He is the Enricher. And he opposed with the sword and the dirham.
Source pages p. 878

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and refutations about divine power (qudra) and human action. The author first dismisses an objection against God as impossible on both theological positions. He then argues that if a single power were adequate for both faith and its opposite, it would be absurd to say it is 'strengthened' for one; rather, divine command and prohibition address the agent. The analogy of the sword and dirham is introduced: just because a sword can kill a friend or an enemy does not mean God gives it for that purpose—rather, it is given for intended use. Power cannot admit both actions; it is created for one specific end. The objection that a sinner acts by God's power is refuted: sin is not attributed to God, and the servant's action is by a power he requests, not by God's power directly. Finally, the objection that if power is created for good, how can one turn it to evil, is answered: power is like a sword, not like heat/cold; it is created for a single purpose and cannot be turned. A human can only ask for power for good; if it did not admit evil, specifying good would be meaningless. The author concludes that power is created for one of them (i.e., either good or evil, but not both for a single action).

Key Terms
القدرة
الفعل
السيف والدرهم
الإعطاء
الامتنان
المعصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that power (qudra) is neutral and can be turned by the agent to either good or evil, implying that God gives a neutral capacity.
Correction: Maturidi argues that power is created specifically for one intended action and cannot be turned; the servant's misuse (e.g., sin) is a result of his own request and choice, not a redirection of the power itself.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it invalid to say that the sinner's action is by God's power?
A) The sinner does not truly act.
B) The power is given for obedience, and the sinner misuses it by his own request.
C) God creates sin directly.
D) The servant acts independently of God.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that divine power is created for a single intended action, not for both good and evil, and that human misuse stems from the servant's own request, not from God's creation of power for evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you blame God for giving you the ability? This lesson shows that the power you misuse was given for a specific good. Will you today repent and recommit every ability you have to its intended purpose—obedience to God?
?
The sword analogy hits home: God gave you power for good, but you turned it to evil. How many times have you used your tongue, your hands, or your wealth in ways God never intended? Will you ask Him now to forgive you and to help you redirect every power back to His service?
?
You claim to believe that all power is from God, but do you live as if every action is a trust? What would change in your next hour if you truly believed that each capability you have is created for one specific good—and that using it otherwise is a betrayal of that trust? Will you act on that belief starting now?

Divine Decree

The Mu'tazilite Argument on Lifespan and Divine Decree
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazilite objection and begins the Sunni answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that a fixed lifespan leads to contradictions in God's power and knowledge.

Core Idea
If God sets a fixed term, murder would imply overpowering God.

The Mu'tazilites argued that if God decrees a precise lifespan for each person, then a murderer who ends that life prematurely would be thwarting God's will. In this passage, Maturidi presents their objection and begins the Sunni response by emphasizing God's absolute knowledge and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite argument
Read the first part of the passage describing their view that God sets a fixed term, and that murder would be a violation of God's promise and power.
Notice the dramatic language: 'breaking the promise, coercion, prevention from His act'.
2
Identify the underlying assumption
The Mu'tazilites assume that if God decrees a term, He must preserve the life until that term, otherwise His power is challenged. Ask: But is this assumption necessary?
3
See the Sunni starting point
Maturidi begins the reply by redirecting to God's knowledge: everything is in His knowledge. If He had willed a different term, it would be in His knowledge, not what occurred.
This shifts the focus from human action to divine omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم سأل عن خصمه سؤالا بتره ، وإنما هو والله أعلم - أن المعتزلة أن الله تعالى يجعل لعمر الرجل مدة بها ينقضى ، وإبقاؤه إلى تلك المدة فعله ، وهو يريد أن يفعل ذلك ، وقد كان قدر له فى تلك المدة أرزاقا أثبت لعبد من عبيد الله قوة يمنع [بها] ذلك الرجل عن استيفاء مدته التي جعلها الله له ، ويمنع رب العالمين عن انجاز ما وعده ويحول بينه وبين فعله من إبقاء حياته فى جسده ، وهو يريد ذلك ليكون من فعله بما يقتله عدوه منعا منه ربه ، فيكون فى ذلك خلف الوعد ، وقهر ومنع عن فعله ، وكل ذلك يكون بما أقدر [0] هو عليه ، وذلك لعجز وخلف وسنة في المعقول أو لا . أجاب الجواب / المسلمين أن المسألة فيما يقال في كل أمر لو لم يكن ذلك كيف كان في علم الله أن يكون ؟ وذلك القول عند المسلمين على تحقيق أن الكائن في علمه ذلك ، فإن كان في علمه وقدرته أن له أن يجعل في الابتداء غير تلك المدة ، ولو جعل ليكون ذلك فى علمه لا هذا الذى كان ، ثم رجع إلى حقيقة قوله وقال : لو كان الظالم إنما قتل الحضور أجله لم يكن معلوما ، وقد يحمد أيضا في ذبح شاة لآخر ، إذ لولا ذبحه لكانت تموت . ثم عورض بأنك تشهد يحضره أجله لو لم يقتله ، فقال : معاذ الله ، بل لعله يقتله غيرى أو ينقضى أجله نية ثم احتج بقوله عز وجل : ( وَلَا يُعَمَّرُ مِنْ مُعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِهِ ) وبقول رسول الله عليه السلام : صلة الرحم تزيد في العمر فأخبر أن له مقدارا
Then he asked his opponent a question that cut him off. It is only that – and God knows best – the Mu'tazila hold that God Almighty sets for a man's lifespan a period by which it ends, and preserving him to that period is His act, and He intends to do that, and He had apportioned for him in that period provisions and established for one of His servants a power to prevent that man from completing his period which God had set for him, and to prevent the Lord of the worlds from fulfilling His promise and to come between Him and His act of preserving his life in his body, while He intends that, so that it would be from his act that his enemy kills him, preventing his Lord [from preserving him], thus resulting in breaking the promise, coercion, and prevention from His act – all that occurs by what He empowered him with, and that is due to incapacity, breach, and a sunna in the intellect or not. The answer of the Muslims: The matter is that it is said in every affair: If it were not for that, how would it be in God's knowledge that it would be? That statement among the Muslims is based on the affirmation that what occurs is in His knowledge. If it was in His knowledge and power that He could have initially made a different period, and if He had made it, that would be in His knowledge, not this which occurred. Then he returned to the reality of his statement and said: If the oppressor only killed the one whose term had already arrived, it would not be known. And one is also praised for slaughtering a sheep for another, for if he did not slaughter it, it would die. Then it was objected: You testify that his term would have arrived if he did not kill him. He said: God forbid, rather perhaps someone else would kill him or his term would end of itself. Then he adduced the saying of God Almighty: 'No one is granted a longer life nor is any life cut short...' and the saying of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: 'Maintaining family ties increases lifespan' – so he informed that it has a measure.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage refutes a Mu'tazilite argument about predestination and the lifespan of a person slain. The opponent argues that if God sets a fixed term for each person, then a murderer would be overpowering God and causing a breach of promise. The Sunni response is that everything occurs within God's knowledge; if God had willed a different term, it would have been. The example of a sheep slaughtered: the slaughterer is praised because the sheep would have died anyway. The objection that the slain would have lived longer is dismissed: perhaps someone else would have killed him or his term would have naturally ended. The Quranic verse (35:11) and hadith about sila ar-rahim increasing lifespan are cited to show that lifespan is decreed but can be changed in God's decree, emphasizing that God's knowledge encompasses all possibilities.

Key Terms
أجل
عمر
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God decrees a lifespan, then murder cuts it short, proving God's decree can be thwarted.
Correction: Maturidi explains that the victim's lifespan is exactly what happens; the murderer is an instrument within God's decree. God's knowledge includes all possibilities, so there is no contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite argument in the passage, if God sets a fixed lifespan for a person, what happens when someone kills that person before the term ends?
A) The murderer overpowers God and breaks His promise.
B) The person dies according to God's will.
C) The lifespan is extended by the murder.
D) God's knowledge changes.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection that a fixed lifespan would allow humans to thwart God is refuted by the Sunni principle that all events are in God's knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of a tragedy in your own life, do you ever feel that someone's evil action 'thwarted' what God wanted for you? How does the Maturidi response that all events are in God's knowledge challenge that feeling? What would it cost you to truly believe that nothing happens outside His knowledge?
?
The Mu'tazilite argument suggests that a fixed term makes God vulnerable to being overpowered. Do you sometimes act as if your choices could 'disappoint' God or alter His plan? Where in your life do you need to surrender the illusion that you can outsmart divine decree?
?
This lesson teaches that the actual event is exactly what God knew and willed. How does that settle your heart about a past regret? Specifically, can you name one thing you wish had been different and, in light of this lesson, say 'But it is in His knowledge, so it is right'? What stops you from doing that now?

Divine Decree
intermediate

The Sunni Response: Evidence from Quran and Hadith
Maturidi refines the answer with an analogy and textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the example of a slaughtered sheep and scriptural evidence to defend the compatibility of divine decree with human action.

Core Idea
Lifespan is decreed but can be 'increased' through God's conditional decree.

After the initial answer based on God's knowledge, Maturidi continues with a concrete example and scriptural proofs. He addresses the objection that the slain person's term would have naturally ended, and then cites the Quranic verse about no increase or decrease in lifespan and the hadith on family ties increasing lifespan, showing that lifespan is subject to divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the continuation of the debate
Read the second part of the passage starting from 'Then he returned to the reality of his statement'.
Notice how Maturidi uses a simple analogy of a sheep.
2
Analyze the analogy of the sheep
He argues that slaughtering a sheep that would have died anyway is praiseworthy. How does this apply to the killer?
The analogy suggests that the killer is an instrument of the predetermined end.
3
Understand the objection and dismissal
The opponent objects that the slain would have lived longer. Maturidi dismisses by saying perhaps someone else would kill him or his term would end naturally.
This shows that the term is not fixed in an absolute sense but in God's knowledge.
4
Examine the scriptural evidence
He cites Quran 35:11 and the hadith on maintaining family ties. These texts seem to say lifespan is fixed yet can be increased. How can both be true?
The key is that the increase is also decreed; it does not contradict God's knowledge.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Write a short summary of how human actions and divine decree are reconciled according to Maturidi.

ثم سأل عن خصمه سؤالا بتره ، وإنما هو والله أعلم - أن المعتزلة أن الله تعالى يجعل لعمر الرجل مدة بها ينقضى ، وإبقاؤه إلى تلك المدة فعله ، وهو يريد أن يفعل ذلك ، وقد كان قدر له فى تلك المدة أرزاقا أثبت لعبد من عبيد الله قوة يمنع [بها] ذلك الرجل عن استيفاء مدته التي جعلها الله له ، ويمنع رب العالمين عن انجاز ما وعده ويحول بينه وبين فعله من إبقاء حياته فى جسده ، وهو يريد ذلك ليكون من فعله بما يقتله عدوه منعا منه ربه ، فيكون فى ذلك خلف الوعد ، وقهر ومنع عن فعله ، وكل ذلك يكون بما أقدر [0] هو عليه ، وذلك لعجز وخلف وسنة في المعقول أو لا . أجاب الجواب / المسلمين أن المسألة فيما يقال في كل أمر لو لم يكن ذلك كيف كان في علم الله أن يكون ؟ وذلك القول عند المسلمين على تحقيق أن الكائن في علمه ذلك ، فإن كان في علمه وقدرته أن له أن يجعل في الابتداء غير تلك المدة ، ولو جعل ليكون ذلك فى علمه لا هذا الذى كان ، ثم رجع إلى حقيقة قوله وقال : لو كان الظالم إنما قتل الحضور أجله لم يكن معلوما ، وقد يحمد أيضا في ذبح شاة لآخر ، إذ لولا ذبحه لكانت تموت . ثم عورض بأنك تشهد يحضره أجله لو لم يقتله ، فقال : معاذ الله ، بل لعله يقتله غيرى أو ينقضى أجله نية ثم احتج بقوله عز وجل : ( وَلَا يُعَمَّرُ مِنْ مُعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِهِ ) وبقول رسول الله عليه السلام : صلة الرحم تزيد في العمر فأخبر أن له مقدارا
Then he asked his opponent a question that cut him off. It is only that – and God knows best – the Mu'tazila hold that God Almighty sets for a man's lifespan a period by which it ends, and preserving him to that period is His act, and He intends to do that, and He had apportioned for him in that period provisions and established for one of His servants a power to prevent that man from completing his period which God had set for him, and to prevent the Lord of the worlds from fulfilling His promise and to come between Him and His act of preserving his life in his body, while He intends that, so that it would be from his act that his enemy kills him, preventing his Lord [from preserving him], thus resulting in breaking the promise, coercion, and prevention from His act – all that occurs by what He empowered him with, and that is due to incapacity, breach, and a sunna in the intellect or not. The answer of the Muslims: The matter is that it is said in every affair: If it were not for that, how would it be in God's knowledge that it would be? That statement among the Muslims is based on the affirmation that what occurs is in His knowledge. If it was in His knowledge and power that He could have initially made a different period, and if He had made it, that would be in His knowledge, not this which occurred. Then he returned to the reality of his statement and said: If the oppressor only killed the one whose term had already arrived, it would not be known. And one is also praised for slaughtering a sheep for another, for if he did not slaughter it, it would die. Then it was objected: You testify that his term would have arrived if he did not kill him. He said: God forbid, rather perhaps someone else would kill him or his term would end of itself. Then he adduced the saying of God Almighty: 'No one is granted a longer life nor is any life cut short...' and the saying of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: 'Maintaining family ties increases lifespan' – so he informed that it has a measure.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage refutes a Mu'tazilite argument about predestination and the lifespan of a person slain. The opponent argues that if God sets a fixed term for each person, then a murderer would be overpowering God and causing a breach of promise. The Sunni response is that everything occurs within God's knowledge; if God had willed a different term, it would have been. The example of a sheep slaughtered: the slaughterer is praised because the sheep would have died anyway. The objection that the slain would have lived longer is dismissed: perhaps someone else would have killed him or his term would have naturally ended. The Quranic verse (35:11) and hadith about sila ar-rahim increasing lifespan are cited to show that lifespan is decreed but can be changed in God's decree, emphasizing that God's knowledge encompasses all possibilities.

Key Terms
أجل
عمر
صلة الرحم
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Sila rahim increases lifespan' contradicts a fixed lifespan.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the increase is within God's decree; the term is not absolutely fixed but determined in God's knowledge as a conditional decree.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue about the sheep slaughtered in the passage?
A) The slaughterer causes its death before its time.
B) The sheep would have died anyway, so the slaughterer is just an instrument.
C) The sheep's lifespan is extended by the slaughter.
D) The slaughterer is not to be praised.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses analogy and scripture to show that human actions do not contradict divine decree; lifespan is decreed in God's knowledge, including any apparent increases.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly trust that every second of your life is measured by God, or do you still secretly fear that your choices can accidentally shorten it?
?
When you try to extend your life through diet, exercise, or medicine, do you see these as independent means or as part of God's decree? How would your daily habits change if you fully internalized Maturidi's teaching?
?
If you knew that your lifespan is already written, would you stop worrying about the future? What is holding you back from that peace?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
The Mu'tazila Dilemma: Does God Break His Promise?
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila argument and the Muslim answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument that if God empowers a servant to kill another, it would lead to God breaking His promise and being coerced, and how Maturidi resolves this through God's knowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge determines what occurs, resolving apparent conflicts in predestination.

Imam al-Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila claim that if God sets a fixed lifespan for a man and then empowers another to kill him, God would be breaking His promise and preventing His own action. He then introduces the Muslim answer: everything that happens is in God's eternal knowledge, so there is no contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila argument
Identify the claim that God's action would be prevented, leading to breach of promise and coercion.
Notice the language of 'خلف الوعد' (breach of promise).
2
Understand the Muslim answer
The answer is that the matter is based on God's knowledge: whatever occurs is exactly what was in His knowledge and power.
This is the key refutation.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: How does God's knowledge resolve the dilemma without attributing injustice to Him?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: وقد حاد عن ذلك؛ إذ القوة لا تحتمل البقاء، وبها أوجب الحاجة، فإذا استحال ذلك لزم ما عورض به عن الغنى، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما قابله به فالوجود لا يديم النفع، بل يديمه البقاء، وله الحاجة إلى الإبقاء، وليس ذلك في القوة؛ فلذلك لزمك الذي تعوذت منه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. تزعم ثم سأل عن خصمه سؤالا بتره، وإنما هو والله أعلم - أن المعتزلة أن الله تعالى يجعل لعمر الرجل مدة بها ينقضي، وإبقاؤه إلى تلك المدة فعله، وهو يريد أن يفعل ذلك، وقد كان قدر له في تلك المدة أرزاقا أثبت لعبد من عبيد الله قوة يمنع ذلك الرجل عن استيفاء مدته التي جعلها الله له، ويمنع رب العالمين عن إنجاز ما وعده ويحول بينه وبين فعله من إبقاء حياته في جسده، وهو يريد ذلك ليكون من فعله بما يقتله عدوه منعا منه ربه، فيكون في ذلك خلف الوعد، وقهر ومنع عن فعله، وكل ذلك يكون بما أقدر هو عليه، وذلك لعجز وخلف وسنة في المعقول أو لا. أجاب الجواب المسلمين أن المسألة فيما يقال في كل أمر لو لم يكن ذلك كيف كان في علم الله أن يكون؟ وذلك القول عند المسلمين على تحقيق أن الكائن في علمه ذلك، فإن كان في علمه وقدرته أن له أن يجعل في الابتداء غير تلك المدة، ولو جعل ليكون ذلك في علمه لا هذا الذي كان، ثم رجع إلى حقيقة قوله وقال: لو كان الظالم إنما قتل الحضور أجله لم يكن معلوما، وقد يحمد أيضا في ذبح شاة لآخر، إذ لولا ذبحه لكانت تموت. ثم عورض بأنك تشهد يحضره أجله لو لم يقتله، فقال: معاذ الله، بل لعله يقتله غيري أو ينقضي أجله نية. ثم احتج بقوله عز وجل: (وَلَا يُعَمَّرُ مِن مُّعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِهِ) وبقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: صلة الرحم تزيد في العمر. فأخبر أن له مقدارا وأنه معلوم يزيد فيه بالصلة، فيكون في اللوح إن وصل فأجله كذا، وإن لم يصل فكذا. ثم رجع إلى سفهه وعارض بالموهوم المطلق. فإن قيل: في ذلك دفع المنع لا غير، وفي القدرة الفعل، فقال: وفي القدرة دفع العجز لا غير لو أوجبت القدرة لأدخلت فيه ولحملت عليه، ويكون إذ ذاك الفعل لغيري. قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله: من تأمل ما قال وما قوبل به أيقن أنه حائد عن حد الجواب، لكنا نذكر غفلته فيما جاد به ليعلموا عذره في فرق به خصومه؛ إذ هذا مبلغ علمه في الله سبحانه. ونقول له: ألله علم أنه يقتل أو لا؟ فإن قال: يعلم، قيل: وقتله يزيل حياته ويذهب عمره أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، كذبه الوجود، وإن قال: نعم، قيل: كيف جعل انقضاء عمره وخروج روحه من جسده بغيره، ولو علم ذلك؟ وكيف كتب في اللوح أنه إن فعل كذا يكون كذا، وإن لم يفعل كذا يكون كذا؟ وهذا أمر من ما يكون، فأما من يعلم ما يكون فهو يكتب: يكون كذا، ولولا أنه يكون كذا، وكذا يكفر فلان ويستوجب مقت الله، ولولا أنه يكفر كان يؤمن ويستوجب محبة الله. فأما القول يكون ذا أو ذا، من غير القطع بما يكون إنما هو فعل الجهال بالعواقب. ثم أنى يكون ذا خبرا عن علم ثبته قبل كونه، وكل الناس يعلمون هذا القدر: إن فلانا إما يقتل أو يموت، يؤمن أو يكفر، يتحرك في وقت كذا أو يسكن. فهذا القدر من اللوح هو لوح كل سفينة وليس هو اللوح المحفوظ، ولكنه اللوح المضيع، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقوله: لو حضر أجله فإن أجله ليس بغير القتل فيما كان في علمه كما في علمه أنه يقتل، ولكنه بالقتل المنهى عنه أو المأمور به على ما في علمه أنه يؤمن ويكفر، فذلك في علمه، وكل داخل على الله، وهو عليم بما يكون. وإن كان في علمه أنه لو لم يفعل ذلك لكان إلى ماذا يرجع، وعلى ذلك فإنه أجل، وكذلك إذ يصل رحمه فجعل عمره أكثر مما كان في علمه أنه لا يصل، وكذلك أمر.
The Sheikh, may God have mercy on him, said: And he deviated from that; for power cannot sustain existence, and by it he necessitated need, so when that is impossible, what he was opposed with regarding wealth becomes necessary, and there is no power but with God. And what he met it with, existence does not perpetuate benefit, but rather perpetuates it through remaining, and he has need for preservation, and that is not in power; therefore, what you sought refuge from is necessary for you, and there is no power but with God. You claim. Then he asked his opponent a curtailed question, and it is only—and God knows best—that the Mu'tazila claim that God Almighty sets for the lifespan of a man a period by which it ends, and keeping him to that period is His action, and He wills to do that, and He had apportioned for him in that period provisions. He established for a servant of God's servants a power by which he prevents that man from completing his period which God has set for him, and prevents the Lord of the worlds from fulfilling His promise, and interposes between Him and His action of preserving his life in his body, while He wills that, so that it would be from His action by that which his enemy kills him, a prevention from his Lord, so in that there is breach of promise, and coercion and prevention from His action, and all that is by that which He empowered him, and that is because of incapacity and breach and custom in the intellect or not? The answer of the Muslims answered that the issue, regarding what is said about every matter: if it were not so, how would it be in God's knowledge that it be? And that saying with the Muslims is based on the verification that what occurs is in His knowledge. For if it is in His knowledge and power that He can make in the beginning other than that period, and if He had made it, it would be in His knowledge not this which occurred. Then he returned to the reality of his statement and said: If the wrongdoer only killed the presence of his term, it would not be known, and he may also be praised for slaughtering a sheep for another, since if he had not slaughtered it, it would die. Then he was objected that you testify that he would have his term if he did not kill him, so he said: God forbid! Rather, perhaps someone else kills him or his term ends by death. Then he argued with His statement, Mighty and Majestic: 'And no one is given a long life nor is his life cut short' and with the statement of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: 'Maintaining family ties increases the lifespan.' So he informed that it has a measure and that it is known, and it increases by the tie, so it would be in the Tablet: if he maintains ties, his term is such, and if he does not maintain ties, it is such. Then he returned to his foolishness and objected with absolute imagination. For if it is said: In that is repelling prevention only, and capacity necessitates action, he said: And capacity necessitates repelling incapacity only, and if capacity necessitated, it would enter into it and be carried upon it, and then the action would be for another. Sheikh Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever contemplates what he said and what was responded to him becomes certain that he is deviating from the limit of the answer, but we mention his negligence in what he argued with so that they know his excuse for his divergence with his opponents; for this is the extent of his knowledge about God, glorified be He. And we say to him: Does God know that he kills or not? If he says: He knows, it is said: Does his killing remove his life and take away his lifespan or not? If he says: No, existence contradicts him, and if he says: Yes, it is said: How did He make the end of his lifespan and the exit of his soul from his body by another, and He knew that? And how did He write in the Tablet that if he does such, it will be such, and if he does not do such, it will be such? And this is a matter of what will be. As for one who knows what will be, he writes: It will be such. And were it not that it will be such, such and such, so-and-so disbelieves and deserves God's wrath, and were it not that he disbelieves, he would believe and deserve God's love. As for the statement 'it will be such or such', without certainty of what will be, it is only the action of the ignorant of outcomes. Then how can this be a report about knowledge that is established before its occurrence? And all people know this extent: that so-and-so either kills or dies, believes or disbelieves, moves at such a time or stays still. This extent of the Tablet is the tablet of every ship, not the Preserved Tablet, but it is the wasted tablet, and there is no power but with God. And his statement: if his term had been present, his term would not be other than the killing, as it is in His knowledge that he kills, but it is by the forbidden killing or the commanded killing, according to what is in His knowledge that he believes or disbelieves, so that is in His knowledge, and everything enters upon God, and He knows what will be. And if it is in His knowledge that if he had not done that, what would his outcome be, and accordingly it is the term. Similarly, if he maintains his family tie, He makes his lifespan more than what was in His knowledge that he would not maintain ties, and similarly the matter.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage is a continuous theological argument by Imam al-Maturidi (rahimahullah) refuting a Mu'tazila position on predestination, lifespan, and God's knowledge. The passage begins with a critique of an opponent who deviated by claiming that power (quwwa) cannot sustain existence (baqa'), and that by power he necessitated need (haja). Maturidi argues that this is impossible, so what the opponent was opposed with regarding wealth (ghina) becomes necessary. He then addresses the opponent's claim directly: 'You claim...' Then Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila argument: that God sets a fixed lifespan for a man, and preserving him to that term is God's action. However, they allege that if God empowers a servant to prevent that man from completing his lifespan, then God would be breaking His promise and being prevented from acting. This leads to absurdities like God being coerced. The Muslim answer is that the matter is based on God's knowledge: if something occurs, it is in God's knowledge. For if it were in God's knowledge and power to make a different term, then that different term would have been the actual one. The opponent then retorts with the example of a murderer killing someone who would have died anyway, and the example of slaughtering a sheep. He also quotes Q. 35:11 and the hadith 'Silat al-rahim increases lifespan' to argue that lifespan is fixed yet increases. Maturidi refutes this by explaining that the Tablet contains conditional statements: 'if he maintains ties, his term is such; if not, such.' He criticizes the opponent for resorting to foolishness and absolute imagination. Then Maturidi delivers his own refutation: He asks the opponent whether God knows that a person will kill or not. If the opponent says 'He knows', then Maturidi asks whether the killing removes his life. If the opponent denies that, reality contradicts him; if he affirms it, then how can God make the end of his life by another while knowing it? Maturidi argues that God writes in the Tablet what will actually happen, not hypotheticals. The statement 'it will be such or such' without certainty is the act of the ignorant. He distinguishes between the common notion of a tablet (lawh kull safina) and the Preserved Tablet (al-lawh al-mahfuz). The opponent's claim is based on a 'wasted tablet'. Finally, Maturidi explains that God's knowledge encompasses both the actual outcome and the hypothetical outcomes (e.g., if he had not killed, what would have happened). The lifespan is tied to God's knowledge, and sadaqah increases it according to what God knows will occur. Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved by understanding that God's eternal knowledge includes all contingencies.

Key Terms
القدرة (power)
العمر (lifespan)
العلم (knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That predestination implies God breaks His promise if He empowers a killer.
Correction: God's knowledge is eternal and comprehensive; what happens is exactly what He knew and willed, so there is no breach of promise.

Checkpoint
According to the Muslim answer in this passage, what determines what actually occurs?
A) Human free will alone
B) God's knowledge and power
C) The actions of angels
D) The Tablet of Destiny

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is the ultimate reality that resolves any apparent conflict between predestination and divine justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When something happens that seems to contradict God's promise or justice, do you immediately assume that God has failed? Or do you pause and recognize that His knowledge encompasses realities you do not see? What would it mean for your relationship with Him if you truly internalized this lesson? Commit today to repeating the phrase 'it is in His knowledge' whenever doubt arises.
?
Think of a time you felt that an evil act 'overpowered' God’s decree. How does this lesson challenge that feeling? If you believe that whatever occurs is exactly what God knew and willed, can you still be angry at the injustice? What would change in your heart if you accepted that even that evil is within His knowledge and wisdom?
?
If you truly believed that every detail of your life—including the actions of others—was in God's knowledge before it happened, what worry would you let go of? What burden would you surrender to Him? Do you dare to live as if that is true today? Write one concrete step you will take to act on this belief.

The Tablet, Conditional Decrees, and God's Knowledge
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila using the hadith on lifespan increase and explains the true nature of the Tablet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila use of the hadith 'Silat al-rahim increases lifespan' by explaining God's knowledge of conditionals and the distinction between the Preserved Tablet and a 'wasted tablet'.

Core Idea
God's knowledge includes both actual outcomes and what would have happened under different conditions.

The Mu'tazila cite the hadith 'Silat al-rahim increases lifespan' to argue that lifespan is not fixed. Maturidi responds by explaining that such conditional increases are already known to God and written in the Tablet accordingly. He then delivers a powerful refutation, distinguishing between the Preserved Tablet and a hypothetical 'wasted tablet' used by those who doubt God's knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's argument from hadith
The opponent claims the hadith proves lifespan can change, contradicting predestination.
Note the verse (Q. 35:11) and hadith quoted.
2
Understand Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi says God writes conditional decrees in the Tablet based on His eternal knowledge.
The Tablet contains conditionals like 'if he maintains ties, his term is such.'
3
Grasp the distinction between tablets
Maturidi distinguishes the 'Preserved Tablet' (al-lawh al-mahfuz) from the 'wasted tablet' of the ignorant.
The wasted tablet represents hypothetical speculations.
4
Reflect on God's knowledge of conditionals
God knows both what will happen and what would have happened if circumstances were different.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

الحاجة إلى الإبقاء، وليس ذلك في القوة؛ فلذلك لزمك الذي تعوذت منه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. تزعم ثم سأل عن خصمه سؤالا بتره، وإنما هو والله أعلم - أن المعتزلة أن الله تعالى يجعل لعمر الرجل مدة بها ينقضي، ويحول بينه وبين فعله من إبقاء حياته في جسده، وهو يريد ذلك ليكون من فعله بما يقتله عدوه منعا منه ربه، فيكون في ذلك خلف الوعد، وقهر ومنع عن فعله، وكل ذلك يكون بما أقدر هو عليه، وذلك لعجز وخلف وسنة في المعقول أو لا. أجاب الجواب المسلمين أن المسألة فيما يقال في كل أمر لو لم يكن ذلك كيف كان في علم الله أن يكون؟ وذلك القول عند المسلمين على تحقيق أن الكائن في علمه ذلك، فإن كان في علمه وقدرته أن له أن يجعل في الابتداء غير تلك المدة، ولو جعل ليكون ذلك في علمه لا هذا الذي كان، ثم رجع إلى حقيقة قوله وقال: لو كان الظالم إنما قتل الحضور أجله لم يكن معلوما، وقد يحمد أيضا في ذبح شاة لآخر، إذ لولا ذبحه لكانت تموت. ثم عورض بأنك تشهد يحضره أجله لو لم يقتله، فقال: معاذ الله، بل لعله يقتله غيري أو ينقضي أجله نية. ثم احتج بقوله عز وجل: (وَلَا يُعَمَّرُ مِن مُّعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِهِ) وبقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: صلة الرحم تزيد في العمر. فأخبر أن له مقدارا وأنه معلوم يزيد فيه بالصلة، فيكون في اللوح إن وصل فأجله كذا، وإن لم يصل فكذا. ثم رجع إلى سفهه وعارض بالموهوم المطلق. فإن قيل: في ذلك دفع المنع لا غير، وفي القدرة الفعل، فقال: وفي القدرة دفع العجز لا غير لو أوجبت القدرة لأدخلت فيه ولحملت عليه، ويكون إذ ذاك الفعل لغيري. قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله: من تأمل ما قال وما قوبل به أيقن أنه حائد عن حد الجواب، لكنا نذكر غفلته فيما جاد به ليعلموا عذره في فرق به خصومه؛ إذ هذا مبلغ علمه في الله سبحانه. ونقول له: ألله علم أنه يقتل أو لا؟ فإن قال: يعلم، قيل: وقتله يزيل حياته ويذهب عمره أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، كذبه الوجود، وإن قال: نعم، قيل: كيف جعل انقضاء عمره وخروج روحه من جسده بغيره، ولو علم ذلك؟ وكيف كتب في اللوح أنه إن فعل كذا يكون كذا، وإن لم يفعل كذا يكون كذا؟ وهذا أمر من ما يكون، فأما من يعلم ما يكون فهو يكتب: يكون كذا، ولولا أنه يكون كذا، وكذا يكفر فلان ويستوجب مقت الله، ولولا أنه يكفر كان يؤمن ويستوجب محبة الله. فأما القول يكون ذا أو ذا، من غير القطع بما يكون إنما هو فعل الجهال بالعواقب. ثم أنى يكون ذا خبرا عن علم ثبته قبل كونه، وكل الناس يعلمون هذا القدر: إن فلانا إما يقتل أو يموت، يؤمن أو يكفر، يتحرك في وقت كذا أو يسكن. فهذا القدر من اللوح هو لوح كل سفينة وليس هو اللوح المحفوظ، ولكنه اللوح المضيع، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقوله: لو حضر أجله فإن أجله ليس بغير القتل فيما كان في علمه كما في علمه أنه يقتل، ولكنه بالقتل المنهى عنه أو المأمور به على ما في علمه أنه يؤمن ويكفر، فذلك في علمه، وكل داخل على الله، وهو عليم بما يكون. وإن كان في علمه أنه لو لم يفعل ذلك لكان إلى ماذا يرجع، وعلى ذلك فإنه أجل، وكذلك إذ يصل رحمه فجعل عمره أكثر مما كان في علمه أنه لا يصل، وكذلك أمر.
The Sheikh, may God have mercy on him, said: And he deviated from that; for power cannot sustain existence, and by it he necessitated need, so when that is impossible, what he was opposed with regarding wealth becomes necessary, and there is no power but with God. And what he met it with, existence does not perpetuate benefit, but rather perpetuates it through remaining, and he has need for preservation, and that is not in power; therefore, what you sought refuge from is necessary for you, and there is no power but with God. You claim. Then he asked his opponent a curtailed question, and it is only—and God knows best—that the Mu'tazila claim that God Almighty sets for the lifespan of a man a period by which it ends, and keeping him to that period is His action, and He wills to do that, and He had apportioned for him in that period provisions. He established for a servant of God's servants a power by which he prevents that man from completing his period which God has set for him, and prevents the Lord of the worlds from fulfilling His promise, and interposes between Him and His action of preserving his life in his body, while He wills that, so that it would be from His action by that which his enemy kills him, a prevention from his Lord, so in that there is breach of promise, and coercion and prevention from His action, and all that is by that which He empowered him, and that is because of incapacity and breach and custom in the intellect or not? The answer of the Muslims answered that the issue, regarding what is said about every matter: if it were not so, how would it be in God's knowledge that it be? And that saying with the Muslims is based on the verification that what occurs is in His knowledge. For if it is in His knowledge and power that He can make in the beginning other than that period, and if He had made it, it would be in His knowledge not this which occurred. Then he returned to the reality of his statement and said: If the wrongdoer only killed the presence of his term, it would not be known, and he may also be praised for slaughtering a sheep for another, since if he had not slaughtered it, it would die. Then he was objected that you testify that he would have his term if he did not kill him, so he said: God forbid! Rather, perhaps someone else kills him or his term ends by death. Then he argued with His statement, Mighty and Majestic: 'And no one is given a long life nor is his life cut short' and with the statement of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: 'Maintaining family ties increases the lifespan.' So he informed that it has a measure and that it is known, and it increases by the tie, so it would be in the Tablet: if he maintains ties, his term is such, and if he does not maintain ties, it is such. Then he returned to his foolishness and objected with absolute imagination. For if it is said: In that is repelling prevention only, and capacity necessitates action, he said: And capacity necessitates repelling incapacity only, and if capacity necessitated, it would enter into it and be carried upon it, and then the action would be for another. Sheikh Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever contemplates what he said and what was responded to him becomes certain that he is deviating from the limit of the answer, but we mention his negligence in what he argued with so that they know his excuse for his divergence with his opponents; for this is the extent of his knowledge about God, glorified be He. And we say to him: Does God know that he kills or not? If he says: He knows, it is said: Does his killing remove his life and take away his lifespan or not? If he says: No, existence contradicts him, and if he says: Yes, it is said: How did He make the end of his lifespan and the exit of his soul from his body by another, and He knew that? And how did He write in the Tablet that if he does such, it will be such, and if he does not do such, it will be such? And this is a matter of what will be. As for one who knows what will be, he writes: It will be such. And were it not that it will be such, such and such, so-and-so disbelieves and deserves God's wrath, and were it not that he disbelieves, he would believe and deserve God's love. As for the statement 'it will be such or such', without certainty of what will be, it is only the action of the ignorant of outcomes. Then how can this be a report about knowledge that is established before its occurrence? And all people know this extent: that so-and-so either kills or dies, believes or disbelieves, moves at such a time or stays still. This extent of the Tablet is the tablet of every ship, not the Preserved Tablet, but it is the wasted tablet, and there is no power but with God. And his statement: if his term had been present, his term would not be other than the killing, as it is in His knowledge that he kills, but it is by the forbidden killing or the commanded killing, according to what is in His knowledge that he believes or disbelieves, so that is in His knowledge, and everything enters upon God, and He knows what will be. And if it is in His knowledge that if he had not done that, what would his outcome be, and accordingly it is the term. Similarly, if he maintains his family tie, He makes his lifespan more than what was in His knowledge that he would not maintain ties, and similarly the matter.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage is a continuous theological argument by Imam al-Maturidi (rahimahullah) refuting a Mu'tazila position on predestination, lifespan, and God's knowledge. The passage begins with a critique of an opponent who deviated by claiming that power (quwwa) cannot sustain existence (baqa'), and that by power he necessitated need (haja). Maturidi argues that this is impossible, so what the opponent was opposed with regarding wealth (ghina) becomes necessary. He then addresses the opponent's claim directly: 'You claim...' Then Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila argument: that God sets a fixed lifespan for a man, and preserving him to that term is God's action. However, they allege that if God empowers a servant to prevent that man from completing his lifespan, then God would be breaking His promise and being prevented from acting. This leads to absurdities like God being coerced. The Muslim answer is that the matter is based on God's knowledge: if something occurs, it is in God's knowledge. For if it were in God's knowledge and power to make a different term, then that different term would have been the actual one. The opponent then retorts with the example of a murderer killing someone who would have died anyway, and the example of slaughtering a sheep. He also quotes Q. 35:11 and the hadith 'Silat al-rahim increases lifespan' to argue that lifespan is fixed yet increases. Maturidi refutes this by explaining that the Tablet contains conditional statements: 'if he maintains ties, his term is such; if not, such.' He criticizes the opponent for resorting to foolishness and absolute imagination. Then Maturidi delivers his own refutation: He asks the opponent whether God knows that a person will kill or not. If the opponent says 'He knows', then Maturidi asks whether the killing removes his life. If the opponent denies that, reality contradicts him; if he affirms it, then how can God make the end of his life by another while knowing it? Maturidi argues that God writes in the Tablet what will actually happen, not hypotheticals. The statement 'it will be such or such' without certainty is the act of the ignorant. He distinguishes between the common notion of a tablet (lawh kull safina) and the Preserved Tablet (al-lawh al-mahfuz). The opponent's claim is based on a 'wasted tablet'. Finally, Maturidi explains that God's knowledge encompasses both the actual outcome and the hypothetical outcomes (e.g., if he had not killed, what would have happened). The lifespan is tied to God's knowledge, and sadaqah increases it according to what God knows will occur. Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved by understanding that God's eternal knowledge includes all contingencies.

Key Terms
صلة الرحم (maintaining family ties)
اللوح (the Tablet)
اللوح المحفوظ (the Preserved Tablet)
اللوح المضيع (the wasted tablet)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith 'Silat al-rahim increases lifespan' contradicts predestination.
Correction: The increase is already known to God and written in the Tablet as a conditional; it does not change God's eternal knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the 'wasted tablet' (اللوح المضيع) a representation of?
A) The actual divine decree
B) The speculative knowledge of the ignorant
C) The actions of angels
D) The fixed lifespan of all creatures

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge encompasses all realities, both actual and conditional, so there is no conflict between hadith on lifespan increase and predestination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God knows not only every action you will ever do, but also every action you would have done if circumstances were different, does that not make you feel a deeper sense of accountability? How will you live today knowing that your potential for both good and evil is fully exposed before Him? Take a moment to repent for any time you secretly wished you had taken a different path—knowing that He knows that wish, and yet still guided you. Will you now trust His decree more completely?
?
The lesson calls those who speak of possibilities without certainty 'ignorant of outcomes.' Are there areas in your life where you still speculate about 'what if'—what if you had made different choices, what if you had not sinned, what if you had died sooner? How does that speculation actually show a lack of trust in God's perfect knowledge and decree? Will you now replace that speculation with gratitude for what He has written for you, knowing that every outcome is precisely what His wisdom required?
?
If God's knowledge includes both your actual sins and the sins you could have committed but didn't, does that not make His mercy even more overwhelming? Think of a time you were spared from a major sin—perhaps by circumstances or by His grace. Can you now see that even that 'near miss' was part of His knowledge and decree, yet He still protected you. How can you use this understanding to deepen your shukr (gratitude) and your fear of displeasing Him, knowing that He knows every possible path you could take?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
Refutation of Conditional Predestination in the Preserved Tablet
Maturidi refutes the claim that the Preserved Tablet contains conditional decrees.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi refutes the idea that the Preserved Tablet contains conditional decrees and how he argues that such a view implies deficiency in God's knowledge and power.

Core Idea
God's decree is absolute and unconditional; conditional predestination implies ignorance.

Maturidi addresses a heretical claim that the Preserved Tablet contains conditional statements about human actions, such as 'if he maintains kinship, his term is such.' This lesson examines Maturidi's refutation, highlighting how the opponent's argument ultimately reduces to absurdity and shows a limited understanding of God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift between the opponent's claim and Maturidi's response.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and Maturidi's initial response
The opponent suggests the Preserved Tablet has conditional statements. Maturidi dismisses this as 'foolishness' and 'absolute illusion'. Ask yourself why he uses such strong language.
3
Understand Maturidi's closing commentary
Imam Abu Mansur (Maturidi) concludes that the opponent has left the proper bounds of response. Reflect on how this shows the opponent's limited knowledge of God.
This connects to the learning objective about deficiency in knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : معلومًا يزيد فيه بالصلة ، فيكون فى اللوح إن وصل فأجله كذا ، وإن لم يصل فكذا . ثم رجع إلى سفهه وعارض بالموهوم المطلق . فإن قيل : في ذلك دفع المنع لا غير ، وفى القدرة الفعل ، فقال : وفى القدرة دفع العجز لا غير لو أوجبت القدرة لأدخلت فيه ولحملت عليه ، ويكون إذ ذاك الفعل لغيري . قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : من تأمل ما قال وما قوبل به أيقن أنه جميع ما أنه حائد عن حد الجواب، لكنا نذكر غفلته فيما جا[د] به ليعلموا عذره في فرق به خصومه ؛ إذ هذا مبلغ علمه في الله سبحانه .
And he said: 'A known thing increased by maintaining kinship, so in the Tablet it would be: if he maintains kinship, his term is such; if he does not maintain it, then such.' Then he returned to his foolishness and objected with absolute illusion. For if it is said: 'In that there is only repelling prevention, and the act is in power,' he said: 'And in power there is only repelling incapacity; if power necessitated [the act], it would be included in it and carried upon it, and then the act would be from another.' Imam Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: 'Whoever ponders what he said and what was responded to with will be certain that all that he [said] is deviating from the bounds of response, but we mention his negligence in what he argued with so that they may know his excuse in the distinction he made with his opponents; for this is the extent of his knowledge concerning God Almighty.'
Source pages p. 881

Commentary
This passage presents an opponent's argument about conditional predestination in the Preserved Tablet, followed by Maturidi's refutation. The opponent claims that the Tablet contains statements like 'if he maintains kinship, his term is such; if not, then such,' implying that God's decree changes based on human actions. Maturidi responds by first noting that the opponent has regressed to foolishness and is objecting with an absolute illusion. The opponent then tries to argue that power only repels incapacity, not that it necessitates the act. Maturidi, in his commentary, states that anyone examining this exchange will see that the opponent has left the proper bounds of response. He notes the opponent's negligence so that readers may understand his excuse and the distinction he makes with his opponents, but ultimately this is the extent of his knowledge about God.

Key Terms
اللوح المحفوظ
الصلة
القدرة
المنع
الجهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human actions such as maintaining kinship can change what is written in the Preserved Tablet.
Correction: Maturidi argues that God's knowledge is eternal and unconditional; conditional decrees imply change in God's knowledge, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the opponent's claim, what does the Preserved Tablet contain?
A) Only fixed decrees without conditions
B) Conditional statements such as 'if he does X, his term is Y'
C) No mention of human actions
D) Instructions for humans to avoid sins

Key Takeaway
Maturidi firmly rejects conditional predestination, affirming that God's decree is certain and unconditional, and any suggestion otherwise stems from ignorance of God's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the opponent claimed God’s decree could change based on your actions, did you feel a secret relief that you might control your fate? How does Maturidi’s refutation expose that feeling as a form of ignorance, and will you now surrender to God’s absolute decree without trying to bargain with Him through your deeds?
?
Consider one area of your life where you often think, ‘If I do this, then God will do that.’ This lesson calls that thinking foolish. Are you willing to release your mental conditional clauses and trust that God’s decree is already perfect, even when you cannot see how your actions fit? What would that trust cost you today?
?
Maturidi says the opponent’s argument shows ‘the extent of his knowledge concerning God.’ Look at your own heart: do you ever secretly believe that God’s knowledge is incomplete until you act? This lesson demands that you repent from that belittling thought. Will you ask God to purify your understanding of His omniscience, no matter how uncomfortable it feels?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
God's Knowledge is Decisive
Maturidi refutes conditional decree with decisive divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi insists that God's knowledge of future events is certain and cannot be expressed in conditional terms.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is absolute; conditional writing would imply ignorance.

Maturidi begins with a direct challenge to those who claim God's decree is conditional. He demonstrates that if God knows an event will occur, then His knowledge is decisive and cannot be expressed as 'if...then...' The Preserved Tablet contains only certain outcomes, not possibilities.

Guided Path
1
Follow the rhetorical question
Read Maturidi's opening question: 'Does God know whether he will be killed or not?' Notice how he forces the opponent to commit to either knowing or not knowing.
The opponent must say God knows; otherwise, it contradicts divine omniscience.
2
Examine the consequence of God's knowledge
If God knows the killing will happen, then that killing ends the person's life. If the opponent denies that, it contradicts observable reality. If he accepts it, then how can God have written conditional statements in the Tablet?
Maturidi argues that one who knows the future writes definitively, not conditionally.
3
Understand the distinction between tablets
Maturidi distinguishes the 'tablet of every ship' (human uncertainty) from the Preserved Tablet. Conditional knowledge is human ignorance, not divine knowledge.
The phrase 'tablet of every ship' refers to ordinary human planning based on guesswork.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول له : الله علم يقتل أو لا ؟ فإن قال : يعلم ، قيل : وقتله يزيل حياته ويذهب عمره أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، كذبه الوجود ، وإن قال : نعم ، قيل : كيف جعل انقضاء عمره وخروج روحه من جسده بغيره ، ولو علم ذلك ؟ وكيف كتب في اللوح أنه إن فعل كذا يكون كذا ، وإن لم يفعل كذا يكون كذا ؟ وهذا أمر من ما يكون ، فأما من يعلم ما يكون فهو يكتب : يكون كذا ، ولولا أنه يكون كذا ، وكذا يكفر فلان ويستوجب مقت الله ، ولولا أنه يكفر كان يؤمن ويستوجب محبة الله . فأما القول بيكون ذا أو ذا، من غير القطع بما يكون إنما هو فعل الجهال بالعواقب . ثم أنى يكون ذا خبرا عن علم ثبته قبل كونه ، وكل الناس يعلمون هذا القدر : إن فلانا إما يقتل أو يموت ، يؤمن أو يكفر ، يتحرك في وقت كذا أو يسكن . فهذا القدر من اللوح هو لوح كل سفينة ولبس هو اللوح المحفوظ ، ولكنه اللوح المضيع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وهو الله ، وقوله : لو حضر أجلة فإن أجله ليس بغير القتل فيما كان في علم كما في علمه أنه يقتل ، ولكنه بالقتل المنهى عنه أو المأمور به على ما في كم في علمه أنه يؤمن ويكفر ، فذلك فى علمه ، وكل داخل على الله ، وهو علم فيما عليم الله عاقبته أنه إلى ماذا ، وإن كان في علمه أنه لو لم يفعل ذلك يرجع ماذا تكون عاقبته أنه إلى ماذا يرجع . وعليه إذ على الله أنه فمثله الأجل . وعلى ذلك إذ يصل رحمهُ فجعل عمره أكثر مما كان في علمه أنه لا يصل ، وكذلك أمر أية ؛ إذ محال أن يكون ما يفعله خارجا من علمه ، والذي قالوا : هو ذلك في المعقول . وللآية قال أهل التأويل : يبين منتهى عمره ، وعلى نقصان كل وقت بمضى من عمره . وقال قوم : إنما هو فى مختلف أعمار الخلق من بين مطول ومقصر ، لا أن الله يجعل لأحد عمرا ثم تبدو له فيزيد أو ينقص كفعل الجهال في أمورهم على شك ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والله تعالى يقول : فَإِذَا جَاء أَجَلُهُمْ لا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةٌ وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ، وفيما يقول لا يجئ أجلهم بل يقتلون قبل مجيء أجلهم . والله أيضا لا يزيد في العمر، وكيف يقدر أن يزيد في عمر آخر بصلة الرحم من لم يقدر بابقاء ما ضمن عمره أن يبقيه إلى وقت كذا ، بل أقدر عدوه حتى منعه عن ذلك ، جل الله عن هذا الوصف .
And we say to him: Does God know whether he will be killed or not? If he says: He knows, it is said: Does his killing remove his life and take away his lifespan or not? If he says: No, existence falsifies him; if he says: Yes, it is said: How did He make the end of his life and the exit of his soul from his body by another, while He knew that? And how did He write in the Tablet that if he does such, it will be such, and if he does not do such, it will be such? This is an affair of what will be. As for one who knows what will be, he writes: It will be such. And if it were not that he will be such, and such, and so-and-so disbelieves and deserves God's wrath, and if it were not that he disbelieves, he would believe and deserve God's love. As for the statement 'it will be this or that,' without certainty of what will be, it is only the action of the ignorant about consequences. Then how can this be a report from knowledge established before its occurrence? And all people know this much: that so-and-so either will be killed or die, believe or disbelieve, move at a certain time or stay still. So this amount from the Tablet is the tablet of every ship, and it is not the Preserved Tablet, but it is the lost tablet, and there is no power except with God. And He is God. And His saying: 'If his term had come, his term is not other than the killing in what was in knowledge, as in His knowledge that he will be killed, but it is by the forbidden or commanded killing according to what is in [unclear] in His knowledge that he believes or disbelieves, so that is in His knowledge, and everything enters upon God, and He knows what God knows its outcome, that it is to what? And if it were in His knowledge that if he did not do that, it would return to what? What would be its outcome that it returns to what? And upon that, since upon God that it is like the term. And upon that, since he maintains his kinship, He made his lifespan more than it was in His knowledge that he would not maintain, and likewise the matter of the verse; for it is impossible that what He does is outside His knowledge. And what they said: that is in the rational. And concerning the verse, the people of interpretation said: He clarifies the end of his term, and upon the decrease of every time by the passing of his lifespan. And some people said: It is only about the different lifespans of creation, between long and short, not that God assigns a lifespan to someone then it becomes apparent to Him to increase or decrease, like the action of the ignorant in their affairs with doubt, and there is no power except with God. And God Almighty says: 'When their term comes, they cannot delay it an hour nor advance it.' And in what He says: their term does not come, but they are killed before the coming of their term. And God also does not increase in lifespan. How can He be able to increase in another's lifespan by maintaining kinship for one whom He was not able to keep alive by preserving what He guaranteed of his lifespan to keep him until a certain time? Rather, He empowered his enemy until he prevented him from that. God is exalted above this description.
Source pages p. 881

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argumentative refutation of the opponent's view that God's decree is conditional. Maturidi begins with a rhetorical question: does God know whether a person will be killed or not? If the opponent says God knows, then the killing ends his life—so the killing is his term. If the opponent denies that killing ends life, that contradicts observable reality. If he accepts it, then how can God write conditional statements in the Tablet? One who knows what will happen writes it definitively. Conditional writing is the act of the ignorant. Maturidi then explains that the kind of uncertainty expressed by 'if he does this, then that' is like the tablet of every ship—a common human ignorance—not the Preserved Tablet. He continues with a discussion of God's saying about the term, clarifying that the term is exactly what God knows, whether by natural death or murder. He refutes the interpretation that maintaining kinship increases lifespan, arguing that God does not change His decree like humans. The verse (7:34) is used to assert that no one dies before or after their term, so the idea that people are killed before their term is false. Maturidi concludes that God is exalted above such changing descriptions.

Key Terms
العلم
اللوح المحفوظ
الجهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God's predestination is conditional, meaning God's knowledge depends on human choices.
Correction: Maturidi asserts that God's knowledge is certain and unconditional; He knows exactly what will happen, so conditional decrees are impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does writing 'if he does such, then such' in the Tablet imply?
A) God's wisdom in planning
B) Ignorance of the outcome
C) That the outcome is undecided
D) That God leaves room for human free will

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is absolute and decisive; conditional decree is incompatible with divine omniscience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face uncertainty in your life, do you catch yourself thinking in 'ifs' and 'maybes' about what Allah has decreed? What does this passage reveal about the root of such thinking, and how can you train your heart to replace it with certainty?
?
This lesson teaches that conditional statements about the future stem from ignorance. Where in your own heart do you harbor conditional thinking about Allah's plan for you—such as 'If I do this, then Allah will give me that'? How can you submit to the decisive knowledge of Allah today?
?
The 'tablet of every ship' is a metaphor for human contingency planning. Look at your own plans and precautions. Are they built on trust in Allah's definitive knowledge, or on anxiety about possibilities? What would it look like to truly believe that Allah already knows and has written every outcome—and to live in light of that certainty?

Divine Decree
intermediate
7 min
The Term (Ajal) is Fixed by God's Knowledge
Maturidi defines the term as fixed by God's knowledge and refutes the idea of conditional changes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi view that every person's term of life is exactly what God knows it to be—whether by natural death or murder—and that no deed can change it.

Core Idea
The term is fixed by God's knowledge; no murder or good deed alters it.

Maturidi now tackles a common question: if God knows everything, can someone be killed before their appointed term? He clarifies that 'term' refers to the exact moment God knows death will occur, whether by natural causes or murder. He also refutes the idea that maintaining kinship can extend one's life, because that would imply change in God's decree.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'term'
Maturidi explains that the term is the moment God knows death will happen. If murder is the cause, then that murder is the term. The Quranic verse (7:34) is used to argue that no one dies before or after the term.
The verse: 'When their term comes, they cannot delay it an hour nor advance it.'
2
Refute the idea of being killed before term
Some claim people are killed before their term. Maturidi says this is false because the killing is the term if God knows it will happen.
The term is defined by God's knowledge, not by apparent cause.
3
Examine the claim that kinship increases lifespan
Maturidi rejects the notion that maintaining kinship adds to one's life. He argues that God's knowledge does not change; the verse about increase refers to the variety of decreed lifespans, not a change in a single person's term.
God is exalted above changing His mind like humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول له : الله علم يقتل أو لا ؟ فإن قال : يعلم ، قيل : وقتله يزيل حياته ويذهب عمره أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، كذبه الوجود ، وإن قال : نعم ، قيل : كيف جعل انقضاء عمره وخروج روحه من جسده بغيره ، ولو علم ذلك ؟ وكيف كتب في اللوح أنه إن فعل كذا يكون كذا ، وإن لم يفعل كذا يكون كذا ؟ وهذا أمر من ما يكون ، فأما من يعلم ما يكون فهو يكتب : يكون كذا ، ولولا أنه يكون كذا ، وكذا يكفر فلان ويستوجب مقت الله ، ولولا أنه يكفر كان يؤمن ويستوجب محبة الله . فأما القول بيكون ذا أو ذا، من غير القطع بما يكون إنما هو فعل الجهال بالعواقب . ثم أنى يكون ذا خبرا عن علم ثبته قبل كونه ، وكل الناس يعلمون هذا القدر : إن فلانا إما يقتل أو يموت ، يؤمن أو يكفر ، يتحرك في وقت كذا أو يسكن . فهذا القدر من اللوح هو لوح كل سفينة ولبس هو اللوح المحفوظ ، ولكنه اللوح المضيع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وهو الله ، وقوله : لو حضر أجلة فإن أجله ليس بغير القتل فيما كان في علم كما في علمه أنه يقتل ، ولكنه بالقتل المنهى عنه أو المأمور به على ما في كم في علمه أنه يؤمن ويكفر ، فذلك فى علمه ، وكل داخل على الله ، وهو علم فيما عليم الله عاقبته أنه إلى ماذا ، وإن كان في علمه أنه لو لم يفعل ذلك يرجع ماذا تكون عاقبته أنه إلى ماذا يرجع . وعليه إذ على الله أنه فمثله الأجل . وعلى ذلك إذ يصل رحمهُ فجعل عمره أكثر مما كان في علمه أنه لا يصل ، وكذلك أمر أية ؛ إذ محال أن يكون ما يفعله خارجا من علمه ، والذي قالوا : هو ذلك في المعقول . وللآية قال أهل التأويل : يبين منتهى عمره ، وعلى نقصان كل وقت بمضى من عمره . وقال قوم : إنما هو فى مختلف أعمار الخلق من بين مطول ومقصر ، لا أن الله يجعل لأحد عمرا ثم تبدو له فيزيد أو ينقص كفعل الجهال في أمورهم على شك ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والله تعالى يقول : فَإِذَا جَاء أَجَلُهُمْ لا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةٌ وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ، وفيما يقول لا يجئ أجلهم بل يقتلون قبل مجيء أجلهم . والله أيضا لا يزيد في العمر، وكيف يقدر أن يزيد في عمر آخر بصلة الرحم من لم يقدر بابقاء ما ضمن عمره أن يبقيه إلى وقت كذا ، بل أقدر عدوه حتى منعه عن ذلك ، جل الله عن هذا الوصف .
And we say to him: Does God know whether he will be killed or not? If he says: He knows, it is said: Does his killing remove his life and take away his lifespan or not? If he says: No, existence falsifies him; if he says: Yes, it is said: How did He make the end of his life and the exit of his soul from his body by another, while He knew that? And how did He write in the Tablet that if he does such, it will be such, and if he does not do such, it will be such? This is an affair of what will be. As for one who knows what will be, he writes: It will be such. And if it were not that he will be such, and such, and so-and-so disbelieves and deserves God's wrath, and if it were not that he disbelieves, he would believe and deserve God's love. As for the statement 'it will be this or that,' without certainty of what will be, it is only the action of the ignorant about consequences. Then how can this be a report from knowledge established before its occurrence? And all people know this much: that so-and-so either will be killed or die, believe or disbelieve, move at a certain time or stay still. So this amount from the Tablet is the tablet of every ship, and it is not the Preserved Tablet, but it is the lost tablet, and there is no power except with God. And He is God. And His saying: 'If his term had come, his term is not other than the killing in what was in knowledge, as in His knowledge that he will be killed, but it is by the forbidden or commanded killing according to what is in [unclear] in His knowledge that he believes or disbelieves, so that is in His knowledge, and everything enters upon God, and He knows what God knows its outcome, that it is to what? And if it were in His knowledge that if he did not do that, it would return to what? What would be its outcome that it returns to what? And upon that, since upon God that it is like the term. And upon that, since he maintains his kinship, He made his lifespan more than it was in His knowledge that he would not maintain, and likewise the matter of the verse; for it is impossible that what He does is outside His knowledge. And what they said: that is in the rational. And concerning the verse, the people of interpretation said: He clarifies the end of his term, and upon the decrease of every time by the passing of his lifespan. And some people said: It is only about the different lifespans of creation, between long and short, not that God assigns a lifespan to someone then it becomes apparent to Him to increase or decrease, like the action of the ignorant in their affairs with doubt, and there is no power except with God. And God Almighty says: 'When their term comes, they cannot delay it an hour nor advance it.' And in what He says: their term does not come, but they are killed before the coming of their term. And God also does not increase in lifespan. How can He be able to increase in another's lifespan by maintaining kinship for one whom He was not able to keep alive by preserving what He guaranteed of his lifespan to keep him until a certain time? Rather, He empowered his enemy until he prevented him from that. God is exalted above this description.

Divine Decree
